Rising crude may hurt corporate profits, markets

https://ucd.idm.oclc.org/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/rising-crude-may-hurt-corporate-profits-markets/docview/1794829947/se-2?accountid=14507

Abstract: A 10% increase in crude oil prices could impact the Ebitda (earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation and amortization) margins of aviation companies by 250-300 basis points, a research analyst at a domestic brokerage said, adding that fuel costs account for 30-35% of airline companies' total costs currently, as compared with 45%-50% a year before.

Links: https://JQ6AM9XS3S.search.serialssolutions.com?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Mint&amp;rft.atitle=Rising+crude+may+hurt+corporate+profits%2C+markets&amp;rft.au=&amp;rft.aulast=&amp;rft.aufirst=&amp;rft.date=2016-06-09&amp;rft.volume=&amp;rft.issue=&amp;rft.spage=&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Mint&amp;rft.issn=&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   Mumbai, June 9 -- With crude oil prices above $50 a barrel and predictions that the worst could be over for oil prices, it could mean bad news ahead for India's economy, its companies and equity markets.
While experts rule out an immediate impact on the economy, they said companies are likely to see a reversal from the trend of margin expansion, as benefits from lower crude prices come off.
Brent crude fell to over a 12-year low of $27.88 per barrel on 20 January. Since then, it has recovered 89.2% to $52.75 per barrel on Thursday, a level last seen on 8 October.
Experts believe the worst is over for oil prices, and commodity prices at large.
Mark Mobius, executive chairman, Templeton Emerging Markets Group, Franklin Templeton Investments, said last month that the worst was probably over for the commodity markets.
"I believe we are now in a recovery phase," Mobius said in an interview, adding that while setbacks weren't ruled out, the situation was definitely better.
"It won't be rapid, it won't be overnight but it would be very good," Mobius said.
Goldman Sachs said in a 15 May report, "The inflection phase of the oil market continues to deliver its share of surprises, with low prices driving disruptions in Nigeria, higher output in Iran and better demand."
"With each of these shifts significant in magnitude, the oil market has gone from nearing storage saturation to being in deficit much earlier than we expected," Goldman Sachs said pegging its West Texas Intermediate crude forecasts at $45 per barrel for the second-quarter of calender year 2016, and $50 per barrel for the second half of 2016.
"...we now expect less downside to oil over 3 months, given supply disruptions, and upgrade commodities to Neutral," Goldman Sachs said in another report on 17 May.
Indian equity markets could also start reacting negatively if crude prices inch higher-while some say $55 per barrel could be the level that would start hurting Indian equity markets, others said the big threat could arrive if oil prices cross $70 per barrel.
"All in all, a range between $40-$50 is still not as bad for India. Beyond that, it will start pinching us on the macroeconomic parameters. Crude prices rising above $55 could start hurting our equity markets, and an increase beyond that level could inversely impact the equity markets," said Amisha Vora, joint managing director of Prabhudas Lilladher Pvt. Ltd.
Some don't see any immediate threat to the markets from the surge in oil prices.
In an interview on 23 May, Jayant Sinha, minister of state for finance pointed that there was not much to worry for the Indian economy until oil crossed $70 per barrel.
"We are a little more sanguine about oil price because every forecast we have seen suggests that oil will remain within $60-70 a barrel. As long as it remains within that range, we are relatively in good shape," Sinha said.
Some analysts agreed.
"The recovery in oil prices after the steep fall has led to risk-on trade. Of course, from the macroeconomic perspective, since we import most of our crude oil requirements, lower prices gel well," said Gautam Chhaochharia, head of research at UBS Securities India Pvt. Ltd.
"That said, crude at $50 a barrel does not really hurt our economy and markets. If crude rises to $60 a barrel, it could lead to first signs of stress, and crude at $70 would start having a negative impact on the markets," said Chhaochharia.
Profit margins of companies which have crude and crude derivatives as their significant raw material components could now see a reversal in trend.
"As far as companies are concerned, the profit margins of those which had crude oil and crude oil derivatives as significant components of their raw material cost, will not enjoy the benefit of such lower costs from here," said Vora.
For airline companies, rising jet fuel costs could start exerting pressure on their operating margins.
A 10% increase in crude oil prices could impact the Ebitda (earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation and amortization) margins of aviation companies by 250-300 basis points, a research analyst at a domestic brokerage said, adding that fuel costs account for 30-35% of airline companies' total costs currently, as compared with 45%-50% a year before. A basis point is one-hundredth of a percentage point.
Government-owned oil marketing companies (OMCs) Indian Oil Corp. Ltd (IOC), Hindustan Petroleum Corp. Ltd (HPCL) and Bharat Petroleum Corp. Ltd (BPCL), which were among the bigger beneficiaries of the lower oil prices, may now start suffering on working capital requirements and consequent interest costs.
Analysts do not see any impact on demand for automobiles at the current level of crude oil prices. However, if crude rises to $70-$75 a barrel, it could start making buyers uneasy.
Tyre makers, who benefitted from lower crude oil prices since a significant portion of their raw material costs are accounted for by crude derivatives products such as synthetic rubber, carbon black, and nylon tyre chord, will now lose out on these benefits.
The paint industry too may face a downside risks to their margins, if the price of crude oil rises.
According to Gautam Duggad, head of research-institutional equities, Motilal Oswal Securities Ltd., crude oil derivatives make up a fourth of raw material costs of paint products.
"If crude oil prices rise, the gross margins of the paint companies have a downside risk as price hikes are staggered and timing difference between crude price rise and price hike in paint products pose downside risks to margins. But, over a period of time, they will be able to pass on the inflation in input costs to consumers," said Duggad.
In a 19 May report, Nomura Financial Advisory and Securities (India) Pvt. Ltd said that Asian Paints Ltd has witnessed significant margin expansion in the last few quarters, mainly driven by weaknesses in crude oil prices, and history suggests that the company's earnings are closely correlated to movements in crude oil prices.
"However, crude prices have stabilised recently, and while margins might expand over the next few quarters due to a lag between import and use, we believe that going forward, expansion will be limited," Nomura analysts said in the note.
The economy at large, of course, is likely to face the brunt first, as India imports around 80% of its crude oil requirements.
"For India, higher oil prices could mean that the bounty showered on it from lower oil prices in terms of a comfortable trade deficit, and almost nil current account deficit, may not continue. With lower crude, rupee was relatively stable, inflation and subsidies were low. With the reversal in oil prices, these will be impacted," said Vora of Prabhudas Lilladher.

THE PRICE of crude oil [fi]: COMMENT [Scot Region]

https://ucd.idm.oclc.org/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/price-crude-oil-fi/docview/1761278698/se-2?accountid=14507

Abstract: Even when you discount one-off items, expenses and accounting effects, BP's net profits are still expected to have fallen 47.4 per cent to $6.4 billion ([Pounds] 4.5 billion). At the same time, its revenues are forecast to have crashed $135.8 billion (Pounds 95.4 billion) to $217.7 billion (Pounds 152.6 billion) according to City analysts.

Links: https://JQ6AM9XS3S.search.serialssolutions.com?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Aeuropeannews&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Express+on+Sunday&amp;rft.atitle=THE+PRICE+of+crude+oil+%5Bfi%5D%3A+COMMENT+%5BScot+Region%5D&amp;rft.au=&amp;rft.aulast=&amp;rft.aufirst=&amp;rft.date=2016-01-31&amp;rft.volume=&amp;rft.issue=&amp;rft.spage=54&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=The+Express+on+Sunday&amp;rft.issn=13660381&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   THE PRICE of crude oil may have gained 25 per cent last week, finishing on Friday at $35.92 (Pounds 25.22) per barrel, but do not think for a second that the crisis that has engulfed the sector is easing. On Tuesday, BP will kick off Big Oil's reporting season and its full-year results are expected to make for grim reading.
Even when you discount one-off items, expenses and accounting effects, BP's net profits are still expected to have fallen 47.4 per cent to $6.4 billion (Pounds 4.5 billion). At the same time, its revenues are forecast to have crashed $135.8 billion (Pounds 95.4 billion) to $217.7 billion (Pounds 152.6 billion) according to City analysts. Arch rival Royal Dutch Shell and other oil majors are expected to show similar profit and revenue slides.
OPEC's price war with American shale producers has seen crude oil fall from $114.80 (Pounds 80.60) per barrel and has resulted in thousands of jobs being lost and scores of multibillion pound projects cancelled. I expect to see thousands more fresh job losses and other cost-cutting measures announced by BP et al when they unveil their results.

Three reasons why crude at $40 can be booster for Indian market [Commodities]

Author: Anand, Kshitij

Publication info: Anand, Kshitij. 

https://ucd.idm.oclc.org/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/three-reasons-why-crude-at-40-can-be-booster/docview/1734392864/se-2?accountid=14507

Abstract: According to the global financial services major, CAD is likely to be about $20.6 billion (1 per cent of GDP) in 2015-16 compared with $28 billion (1.4 per cent of GDP) last year.

Links: https://JQ6AM9XS3S.search.serialssolutions.com?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Economic+Times&amp;rft.atitle=Three+reasons+why+crude+at+%2440+can+be+booster+for+Indian+market+%5BCommodities%5D&amp;rft.au=Anand%2C+Kshitij&amp;rft.aulast=Anand&amp;rft.aufirst=Kshitij&amp;rft.date=2015-11-20&amp;rft.volume=&amp;rft.issue=&amp;rft.spage=&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=The+Economic+Times&amp;rft.issn=09718680&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   NEW DELHI: The domestic equity market has managed to outperform other emerging markets (EMs) so far in calendar 2015, largely because of improved economic fundamentals and a crash in commodities, including crude prices. "India's long-term structural story seems intact. Within the emerging markets pack as a whole, we clearly stand out," says Mayuresh Joshi, Fund Manager, Angel Broking. India imports over 70 per cent of its crude requirement and, thus, falling crude oil prices would ease current account deficit and also significantly reduce the fuel subsidy burden, experts said. The expenditure on crude oil accounts for 30 per cent of India's import bill. "India is not exposed to the commodities universe unlike a number of other emerging markets, such as Brazil or Russia. Plus, the reform processes is also coming through. Some green shoots are probably evident in terms of how the project wins and project initiations have started at least on the government side," Joshi said. He said the market might remain largely rangebound over the next few months, but still India remains in a sweet spot. The slowdown in global economies has impacted the demand side, which has resulted in a sharp drop in crude oil prices. But the India is net importer of crude oil. So any drop in crude price is beneficial for the domestic economy as our import bill goes down and the subsidy burden drops significantly. Speaking at an event in the United Arab Emirates (UAE), finance minister Arun Jaitley recently said low crude prices have created a favourable environment for the Indian economy, as it has helped absorb the loss faced by public sector oil marketers and also contributed to the fall in inflation. The near 40 per cent correction in crude prices so far in calendar 2015 to about $40 a barrel has been largely on account of a slowdown in the Chinese economy, as well as a supply glut. "More than China, supply factors have played a larger role than demand factors in driving crude prices lower. The higher oil output was mainly because of non-OPEC developments such as a US shale gas boom and also higher-than-expected OPEC output in countries such as Iraq, Libya and Saudi Arabia," said Nikhil Kamath, Director, Trading & Risk- Zerodha. The crash in crude prices has been in tandem with the slowdown in the global economy, which has only expedited the fall. "No one factor can influence the direction of an economy as mammoth as ours, but we should definitely not ignore the fact that despite all the turmoil, India is outperforming most foreign economies at a healthy pace," he said. Sanjay Guglani, CEO, Silverdale Capital, said the basic reason why India has not gone through so much of pain is mainly because of the drop in commodity prices, specifically in crude prices. "One has to look at it in terms of medium-term to long-term plays and when the structural reforms take place," he said. We have collated a list of three factors that will aid the market going forward: Improvement in CAD: India is a major importer of petroleum crude. Crude prices have declined 42.6 per cent over the past year, which has had a significant positive impact on India's current account deficit. With the decline in crude prices on an annualised basis, India's imports have fallen 21.2 per cent in October 2015 to $31.1 billion compared with $39.5 billion in the year-ago period. Official figures show trade deficit in the first seven months of the financial year (April-October) has shrunken to $77.76 billion compared with $86.26 billion in the last financial year. "Lower crude oil prices will be certainly good for the Indian economy, as India imports nearly two-thirds of its crude oil requirements, spending $130 billion annually to meet its burgeoning oil demand," said D K Aggarwal, CMD, SMC Investments and Advisors. Going forward, India's current account deficit (CAD) is likely to be about 1 per cent of the GDP in the current financial year because of low crude prices and contained gold imports, Citigroup said in a report. According to the global financial services major, CAD is likely to be about $20.6 billion (1 per cent of GDP) in 2015-16 compared with $28 billion (1.4 per cent of GDP) last year. "Though it's still early to call the bottom on export contraction, we maintain our view that India's current account deficit will shrink to around 1 per cent of GDP in FY16 due to low crude oil prices and contained gold imports," Citigroup said in a research note. Sectors that will benefit: A fall in crude oil prices is particularly beneficial for sectors that use crude and crude derivatives as a raw material. Stocks of sectors such as paint, tyre, FMCG, airlines and lubricants will remain in focus. "Sectors such as paint, adhesives, insecticides and specialty chemicals use many key raw materials that are correlated to crude oil prices," says Tushar Pendharkar, Head of Research at Right Investment Advisory Services. "Thus lower crude prices can sustain higher operating margins for companies in these sectors. In addition, heavy industries such as metals, cement, engineering and capital goods can sustain the control over power and fuel expenses," he said. Oil and gas upstream companies, independent oil explorers and oil rig operators would be impacted if crude prices stay at current levels for a long time. "The universe of stocks that will get impacted negatively is smaller compared with the number beneficiaries of lower crude oil prices," said Jimeet Modi of SAMCO Securities. "Stocks like Cairn India, ONGC, GAIL, Oil India, Reliance Industries and Aban Offshore are likely to be affected adversely if crude oil prices stay at these levels," he said. Outlook for crude oil: Crude oil will largely remain flat or hover around these levels with a slightly bullish bias, say experts. Commodities take far longer to bottom out as the demand-supply equilibrium needs to turn around, they say. Lower crude oil prices for the rest of the year would mean more strength in the macro-economy, which would act as a key to attracting foreign money. "Supplies need to get absorbed while new supplies are not forthcoming due to low or no investment in exploration activities in the past. Generally, crude oil has a habit of consolidation of about two to three years before the prices turn up," said Modi of SAMCO Securities. Analysts expect crude oil to remain under pressure and move in a range over the next 12 months. But the $40-50 a barrel price level is very low to sustain, and it should ideally move higher, because for most of the oil producing countries, $80-90 is the break-even point. "At current level, oil could benefit India in the short run. However, it won't help achieve strong economic performance in the long run. For most of the oil-producing countries, $80-90 is the BEP (breakeven point) and thus I believe oil would roam around this level in long run," said Pendharkar. Kamath of Zerodha expects crude prices to remain in the $ 35-55 range over the next 12 months. Apart from that US Fed rate cycle, geopolitical concerns are some of the factors that could affect future crude price trends.

Polish avg. retail gasoline prices keep falling w w in week ending Sept. 3, to move further down: Retail prices continued to fall - to the lowest level since mid-April in the case of Eu 95 - despite wholesale price increases caused by USD PLN growth and volatility in crude oil prices, Reflex commented.

Author: Minda, Alicja

Publication info: Minda, Alicja.

Abstract: Retail prices continued to fall - to the lowest level since mid-April in the case of Eu 95 - despite wholesale price increases caused by USD PLN growth and volatility in crude oil prices, Reflex commented.

Big gains likely for Indian firms as Iran pumps more oil; crude prices may drop $4/barrel [Oil & Gas]

Author: Prasad, Rachita; Choudhary, Sanjeev; Sahgal, Ram

Publication info: Prasad, Rachita; Choudhary, Sanjeev; Sahgal, Ram. 

https://ucd.idm.oclc.org/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/big-gains-likely-indian-firms-as-iran-pumps-more/docview/1696054129/se-2?accountid=14507

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://JQ6AM9XS3S.search.serialssolutions.com?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Economic+Times&amp;rft.atitle=Big+gains+likely+for+Indian+firms+as+Iran+pumps+more+oil%3B+crude+prices+may+drop+%244%2Fbarrel+%5BOil+%26amp%3B+Gas%5D&amp;rft.au=Prasad%2C+Rachita%3BChoudhary%2C+Sanjeev%3BSahgal%2C+Ram&amp;rft.aulast=Prasad&amp;rft.aufirst=Rachita&amp;rft.date=2015-07-15&amp;rft.volume=&amp;rft.issue=&amp;rft.spage=&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=The+Economic+Times&amp;rft.issn=09718680&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   MUMBAI: Iran on Tuesday reached an agreement on its nuclear programme with six world powers led by the US, a development that could end a nearly four-decade-old standoff with the West. The agreement limits Iran's nuclear capabilities for a decade and puts in place a tighter inspection regime in return for lifting financial and military sanctions.
Indian oil firms, especially upstream players such as ONGC and Oil India, could be in for big gains as Iran is likely to pump more crude oil into an already surplus market, pushing prices even lower.
Intraday benchmark Brent prices fell $1.07 to $56.78 a barrel. Experts said crude may fall $3-4 more as supply increases even as demand growth remains muted.
Oil and gas shares in India reacted positively, with refiners leading the pack. The S&P BSE Oil and Gas Index ended up 0.6 per cent at 9963.05 while the benchmark Sensex closed down 0.1 per cent. Indian Oil Corp and Hindustan Petroleum Corp gained over 3 per cent while Bharat Petroleum shares ended up 2 per cent.
"Iranian production is expected to increase by close to 0.5 million barrels per day in six months which will result in a crude price impact of close to $3 per barrel. This, in turn, will lead to underrecovery declining by Rs 3,600 crore and upstream company realisations will improve by Rs 1,200 crore. There will be no material impact on oil marketing companies," said Rahul Prithiani, director, CRISIL Research.
India, which used to source over 10 per cent of its crude requirements from Iran with Essar Oil and Mangalore Refinery being the biggest importers, has been reducing shipments from that country in response to sanctions by the West.
India's oil imports from Iran declined in January-June this year by 23 per cent as companies curbed inbound shipments. Indian oil refiners have stepped up purchases from other geographies such as Mexico, Iraq and Venezuela while building inventories as crude prices remain weak due to lower demand. Industry watchers said refiners are now likely to renew shipments from Iran.
An oil ministry official said: "We will have to see the details of the deal before taking a view. There is no dearth of crude oil in the world. Iran was attractive mainly because of its sops. The sops will now very likely disappear. So we will have to weigh if it makes economic sense to import from Iran." The lifting of the ban now puts pressure on Indian refiners to resume payments to Iran for their past buys. They owe about $6.5 billion to Iran for oil imports, which is about 55 per cent of the bill for crude sourced since February 2013, when payments through Turkey's Halkbank were stopped due to sanctions by the West.
"I think the payment will have to be made in a staggered manner and our companies are ready for that," the oil ministry official said. Commenting on ONGC's interest in Iranian blocks, he said, "We were already engaged with Iran on this. Now we will push them to expedite this."
 
COMMERCIAL TERMS TO BE KEY
An executive at Indian Oil Corp, which imported less than a million tonnes from Iran last fiscal year, said: "Whether imports from Iran will rise or fall will depend entirely on commercial terms. We are a minor importer of Iranian crude and will take a view on future trade purely on the basis of its economics."
On the commodity bourse MCX, traders have begun building bearish bets on crude oil futures, expecting a further decline in price. Intraday crude on MCX was down by almost 3 per cent at Rs 3,250 a barrel. The open interest or outstanding traders' positions were up at 21,189 contracts from 14,565 contracts a day ago, implying the creation of fresh short positions, said Sriram Iyer, analyst, Admisi Commodities.
Chirag Shah, senior vice-president at Phillip Commodities, a subsidiary of Singapore-based Phillip Capital, said his firm's overseas parent was advising clients to buy Brent and sell US crude (WTI) in anticipation of a widening spread between the two crude grades post the Iran deal.
Intraday Tuesday, Brent traded at $56.78 a barrel versus WTI's $51.13 - a spread of $5.65. Shah expects this spread to widen as Iranian oil is heavier and more sour than Brent and WTI. While both WTI and Brent would decline, the former - whose physical usage is comparatively lesser than Brent - would fall more sharply. "The spread could thus potentially widen the way it did on February 27 - to as much as $12.82 from the current level ($5.62). It's a good strategy to buy the spread, by putting a stop loss in place to limit losses in case the trade goes awry," said Shah.

The impact of falling crude oil prices

https://ucd.idm.oclc.org/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/impact-falling-crude-oil-prices/docview/1694858273/se-2?accountid=14507

Abstract: [...]the outlook on crude oil prices is subdued, with expectations of weak demand from China as well as Europe. [...]a potential threat hangs over the oil market from the easing of sanctions against Iran and the resultant increase in supplies in the global oil market.

Links: https://JQ6AM9XS3S.search.serialssolutions.com?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Mint&amp;rft.atitle=The+impact+of+falling+crude+oil+prices&amp;rft.au=&amp;rft.aulast=&amp;rft.aufirst=&amp;rft.date=2015-07-08&amp;rft.volume=&amp;rft.issue=&amp;rft.spage=&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Mint&amp;rft.issn=&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   New Delhi, July 8 -- Brent crude oil prices have dropped by 17% to around $57 per barrel from the year's high of $69.02 a barrel on 6 May.
But despite that steep decline, Brent continues to trade 7% higher from the year's low of $53.52 a barrel reached on 20 January.
Nevertheless, the outlook on crude oil prices is subdued, with expectations of weak demand from China as well as Europe.
Moreover, a potential threat hangs over the oil market from the easing of sanctions against Iran and the resultant increase in supplies in the global oil market.
What is the impact of falling crude prices for India?
The gains from lower inflation, a lower current account and a smaller subsidy burden are well known.
For the market, what matters is the impact on corporate earnings. Oil marketers Bharat Petroleum Corp. Ltd (BPCL), Hindustan Petroleum Corp. Ltd (HPCL) and Indian Oil Corp. Ltd (IOCL) are expected to benefit from falling crude oil prices as their overall losses from selling fuel below cost diminish. Stocks of these three oil marketing companies have anyway outperformed the BSE Sensex index since the beginning of 2015 itself, helped by a decline in under-recoveries, better refining margins and expansion of marketing margins.
Aviation companies and lubricant makers, too, benefit when crude oil prices decline on account of cost benefits. Shares of Jet Airways (India) Ltd and Castrol India Ltd were marginally up on Wednesday, on a day the benchmark BSE Sensex ended 1.7% lower.
On the other hand, lower crude prices will mean that net price realizations of state-run upstream companies such as Oil and Natural Gas Corp. Ltd (ONGC) and Oil India Ltd (OIL) will face downward pressure. A lack of clarity on a transparent subsidy sharing mechanism continues to remain a worry for these stocks. Not surprisingly, shares of ONGC and OIL have underperformed so far in 2015.
In general, falling crude oil prices tend to adversely affect refining margins (due to inventory losses), which may affect Indian refiners to that extent. Cairn India Ltd, the so-called direct crude play in the country, shed 4% (adjusting for dividend) on Wednesday on concerns of falling crude oil prices. In 2015, Cairn India shares have lost about 28%, thanks to lower crude oil prices and the Vedanta-Cairn merger announcement. So far in 2015, the Brent crude price has declined by 7%.
Published by HT Syndication with permission from MINT.

Europe little changed despite Iraq news: Stocks tread water while crude oil prices spike on news of escalating violence Aer Lingus and Ryanair again dragged down a sector-wide slide in airline stock

Market Focus: European Drivers Get Smaller Boost at the Pump

Author: Gross, Jenny

Publication info: Gross, Jenny. 

https://ucd.idm.oclc.org/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/market-focus-european-drivers-get-smaller-boost/docview/1022231677/se-2?accountid=14507

Abstract: [Brent] crude-oil prices last week hit their lowest level in 18 months. Industry experts say prices could slide even more if the global picture worsens. At Monday's low of $89.60 a barrel, Brent crude oil in dollar terms had fallen 30% after hitting its year-to-date high on March 1. In euros, Brent crude oil has fallen 22% to 73.63 euros, while in pounds, oil had fallen 26% to GBP 58.37. "Even though there has been a very welcome drop in the price of wholesale fuel, it hasn't been as widely beneficial as it might have been four years ago because at that time the pound sterling bought $2," he said. "Today it has weakened quite rapidly and now only buys you $1.55." "On a percentage basis, obviously the U.S. price is more directly correlated with the price of crude oil than Europe since only 11% is accounted for by taxes," he said. "So when you see movement in crude oil, it accounts for a smaller share of pump prices in Europe than in the U.S."

Links: https://JQ6AM9XS3S.search.serialssolutions.com?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Aeuropeannews&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;rft.atitle=Market+Focus%3A+European+Drivers+Get+Smaller+Boost+at+the+Pump&amp;rft.au=Gross%2C+Jenny&amp;rft.aulast=Gross&amp;rft.aufirst=Jenny&amp;rft.date=2012-06-27&amp;rft.volume=&amp;rft.issue=&amp;rft.spage=25&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;rft.issn=09219986&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text: European motorists are still waiting to reap the full benefits of crude oil's recent slide as a weak euro, U.S. buying and high taxes keep gasoline prices high.
The situation is compounding the misery for European economies, already in recession, making it less likely that falling oil prices can stimulate business and consumer spending and drive growth.
Since the beginning of April, U.S. gasoline prices have tumbled 10% to $3.59 a gallon, but prices on average in Europe have fallen just 5.5%, to an average of 1.67 euros ($2.09) per liter, according to statistics from the U.S. Department of Energy and the European Commission, respectively, for the week ended Monday.
Analysts blame stubbornly high European gasoline prices on the weakness of the euro and pound relative to the dollar. As the euro weakens, purchasing cargoes of gasoline on the international market, which is priced in dollars, is more expensive for Europeans.
Since early April, the euro has fallen 6.2% to $1.25 as Spanish bond yields have soared and Europe's overall economic outlook has worsened.
During that period, prices for Brent crude, the international oil benchmark, have slumped more than $32, or 26%, to $92.96 a barrel.
Brent crude-oil prices last week hit their lowest level in 18 months. Industry experts say prices could slide even more if the global picture worsens. At Monday's low of $89.60 a barrel, Brent crude oil in dollar terms had fallen 30% after hitting its year-to-date high on March 1. In euros, Brent crude oil has fallen 22% to 73.63 euros, while in pounds, oil had fallen 26% to GBP 58.37.
Brian Madderson, chairman of the U.K.'s Retail Motor Industry Federation, which represents independent gas-station operators, said currency weakness is exacerbating fuel costs for drivers.
"Even though there has been a very welcome drop in the price of wholesale fuel, it hasn't been as widely beneficial as it might have been four years ago because at that time the pound sterling bought $2," he said. "Today it has weakened quite rapidly and now only buys you $1.55."
In addition to the euro's weakening relative to the dollar, demand for gasoline in the U.S. is pulling the product out of Europe and keeping prices strong, said Thina Saltvedt, senior oil market analyst at Nordea Bank Norge.
"That's basically pushed up [European gasoline] prices more than crude oil prices should suggest," she said.
To make matters worse for European drivers, taxes comprise an average of 52% of gasoline and diesel prices across the Continent, according to figures from Eurogeographic. The comparable May figure for the U.S. was 11%, according to the U.S. Energy Information Administration.
This means that on average in Europe, a lower percentage of the cost of gasoline is for the fuel itself than in the U.S.
"In European Union countries, such a huge chunk of the price is tax," said Simon Wardell, energy research manager at IHS Global Insight. "The knock-on effects are much more modest in terms of what end-user consumers see."
Jonathan Cogan, a spokesman for the EIA, said the U.S. has seen 12 straight weeks of declining gasoline prices, the result of the falling price of crude.
"On a percentage basis, obviously the U.S. price is more directly correlated with the price of crude oil than Europe since only 11% is accounted for by taxes," he said. "So when you see movement in crude oil, it accounts for a smaller share of pump prices in Europe than in the U.S."
Luke Bosdet, a spokesman for the U.K.'s Automobile Association, said it takes about two weeks for changes in crude oil prices to filter into prices at the pump in the U.K.
He said that in the U.K., the reason why prices haven't come down as much is because gasoline retailers here have been deliberately slow to lower prices according to the drop in crude oil prices.
---
Peter Evans in London contributed to this article.

Global markets to remain volatile on Gulf unrest, crude oil [Financial Times]

Author: Agarwal, Vikas

Publication info: Agarwal, Vikas. 

https://ucd.idm.oclc.org/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/global-markets-remain-volatile-on-gulf-unrest/docview/857780765/se-2?accountid=14507

Abstract: Analysts believe a prolonged crisis and its spread to other countries can worsen the situation in the global economy with respect to crude oil price in the international markets. The rising crude oil price will work as double edged sword - if the government controls the price of retail fuel in the market the fiscal deficit will go up, while if it lets the price free for the market to decide the inflation rate will go up.

Links: https://JQ6AM9XS3S.search.serialssolutions.com?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Economic+Times&amp;rft.atitle=Global+markets+to+remain+volatile+on+Gulf+unrest%2C+crude+oil+%5BFinancial+Times%5D&amp;rft.au=Agarwal%2C+Vikas&amp;rft.aulast=Agarwal&amp;rft.aufirst=Vikas&amp;rft.date=2011-03-21&amp;rft.volume=&amp;rft.issue=&amp;rft.spage=&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=The+Economic+Times&amp;rft.issn=09718680&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text: The political tensions in the gulf region are going on from the last couple of months. It started with the protests against dictatorial regimes. The protestors are demanding democratic governance which means the end of long-run dictatorial regimes.
The protests started in Tunisia a few months ago and spread to Egypt and Libya. International agencies and developed nations have not intervened actively but are passively supporting the move for democratic governance.
The supply of crude oil is the first to be affected whenever anything adverse happens in the gulf region. The gulf countries produce a large part of global crude oil demand and drive the global economy with respect to the energy requirements.
Although Libya's crude oil production is not very significant (around two percent of the total OPEC output), the main cause of worry is the prolonged tensions and spread of this movement to other gulf countries.
The price of crude oil has already shot up last year due to the rise in demand from emerging nations and unavailability of any appropriate substitute for crude oil. Analysts believe a prolonged crisis and its spread to other countries can worsen the situation in the global economy with respect to crude oil price in the international markets.
Impact on global markets
In general, the markets are very sensitive to global news and developments. The markets are closely following the developments around these political tensions in the gulf countries, especially due to their control on crude oil reserves.
There is a lot of volatility in the markets based on the news from the gulf region. The global markets are expected to remain nervous, going forward, even if the Libyan crisis subsides, due to speculations on the protests spreading to other gulf countries.
Impact on commodities
The crisis in the gulf region is directly linked to escalation in price of crude oil which has gone above 100 dollars per barrel. The high price of crude oil is a cause for concern for countries such as India which are dependent on imports to fulfil their crude oil requirements . In case the crude oil price rises sharply, it will have a serious impact.
In India, the government is controlling the prices of diesel, kerosene and cooking gas to shield the consumers from volatility in crude oil price. The rising crude oil price will work as double edged sword - if the government controls the price of retail fuel in the market the fiscal deficit will go up, while if it lets the price free for the market to decide the inflation rate will go up.
Gold and silver have volatile movements during uncertain times at the global level. Large funds and investors invest in precious metals to hedge and lower risk in their portfolios against the global uncertainties . The prices of gold and silver have already shot up to record levels and analysts believe they have the potential to rise further if the gulf crisis spreads to other countries in the region.

Significant developments investors need to track [Financial Times]

Author: Agarwal, Vikas

Publication info: Agarwal, Vikas. 

https://ucd.idm.oclc.org/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/significant-developments-investors-need-track/docview/855141443/se-2?accountid=14507

Abstract: If the policymakers control the price of retail fuel in the market, the fiscal deficit goes up, while if they let the price free for the market to decide, the inflation rate goes up. [...] the domestic markets are following the movements of crude oil price in the international markets closely.

Links: https://JQ6AM9XS3S.search.serialssolutions.com?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Economic+Times&amp;rft.atitle=Significant+developments+investors+need+to+track+%5BFinancial+Times%5D&amp;rft.au=Agarwal%2C+Vikas&amp;rft.aulast=Agarwal&amp;rft.aufirst=Vikas&amp;rft.date=2011-03-07&amp;rft.volume=&amp;rft.issue=&amp;rft.spage=&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=The+Economic+Times&amp;rft.issn=09718680&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text: The domestic markets went through a strong rally last week after the better-than-expected Union Budget presented by the Finance Minister on Monday. The Budget delivered pleasant surprises related to the fiscal deficit target which raised the confidence level in the markets. However, the markets remained nervous towards the end of the week due to the crisis in Libya and the sharp rise in the crude oil price.
Going forward, in the short term, the markets are expected to be driven mainly by global developments and investors should track the significant global events. In the Forex market, the rupee gained strength against the dollar and came down to around Rs 45 per dollar. In the commodity markets, gold and silver touched their all-time highs last week due to the tension in the north African region.
These are some of the major events expected to drive the market sentiments and direction in the short to medium terms:
Crisis in Libya
The crisis in Libya appeared to cool down towards the beginning of the week after the statements from some large economies. However, fresh tension cropped up in the region towards the middle of the week which again increased the nervousness in the markets.
The markets are nervous on the possible spread of the crisis to other countries in the West Asian and north African regions that command a large part of the crude oil reserves. Due to its impact on the crude oil price movements, this issue is very significant for the market sentiments.
Volatility in crude oil price
The volatility in the crude oil price continued last week, around the Libyan crisis.
The crude oil price is hovering close to the 100 dollars per barrel mark. The rising crude oil price is a cause for concern. India imports more than 70 percent of the crude oil requirements and the government is controlling the prices of diesel, kerosene and cooking gas.
In case the crude oil price rises sharply, it could have a serious impact. If the policymakers control the price of retail fuel in the market, the fiscal deficit goes up, while if they let the price free for the market to decide, the inflation rate goes up.
Therefore, the domestic markets are following the movements of crude oil price in the international markets closely.
US data positive
Positive news and signals continued to come out of the largest economy on the globe. The US government's report showed the number of people filing for fresh unemployment benefits dropped to the lowest since May 2008 at 3.68 lakhs.
On the other hand, the retailers in the US reported strong top line numbers for the month of February, thereby extending the strong spending momentum of the holiday season. The positive economic developments in the US are definitely good for the global economy and could fuel positive sentiments in the global markets.
Union Budget
The Finance Minister presented a safe Budget last week. However, it lacked many expected reforms measures. The Finance Minister continued his focussed spending on infrastructure, agriculture and education sectors. Measures to control shortterm inflation were missing in the Budget. Also, the Budget had no major announcements related to real reforms.
The Budget impressed the markets on the fiscal deficit front. The budgeted fiscal deficit of 4.6 percent for the financial year 2012 is way below the market's expected target of 4.8 percent, and surprised the markets pleasantly. The Budget has created positive sentiments in the markets but it would be important to assess its realisation, going forward.

LITRE OF FUEL UP 10P: LIBYA TURMOIL PUMPS UP PRICE OF CRUDE OIL

Author: Hiscott, Graham

Publication info: Hiscott, Graham. 

https://ucd.idm.oclc.org/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/litre-fuel-up-10p/docview/853626282/se-2?accountid=14507

Abstract: Rocketing oil prices thanks to the Libyan unrest and a Coalition duty increase could see unleaded hit nearly pounds 1.39 a litre and diesel more than pounds 1.44 within weeks.

Links: https://JQ6AM9XS3S.search.serialssolutions.com?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Aeuropeannews&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Daily+Mirror&amp;rft.atitle=LITRE+OF+FUEL+UP+10P%3A+LIBYA+TURMOIL+PUMPS+UP+PRICE+OF+CRUDE+OIL&amp;rft.au=Hiscott%2C+Graham&amp;rft.aulast=Hiscott&amp;rft.aufirst=Graham&amp;rft.date=2011-02-24&amp;rft.volume=&amp;rft.issue=&amp;rft.spage=6&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=The+Daily+Mirror&amp;rft.issn=&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text: MOTORISTS are being warned to brace themselves for a 10p a litre surge at the pumps.
Rocketing oil prices thanks to the Libyan unrest and a Coalition duty increase could see unleaded hit nearly pounds 1.39 a litre and diesel more than pounds 1.44 within weeks.
The news will come as a blow to millions of drivers already reeling from record high fuel costs.
Oil hit a two-year high of $112 (pounds 69) a barrel yesterday amid fears Middle East chaos will spread. Up to 25% of Libya's oil production has been shut down during the strife.
Trade body RMI Retail said the surge was likely to feed through to a 5p a litre rise in forecourt prices.
And it warned prices would jump another 5p a litre on April 1 if the Tory-led Government pressed ahead with its duty and VAT rises.
RMI Retail chairman Brian Madderson said: "We once again urge the Government to abandon plans to introduce this fuel duty escalator. Windfall tax from North Sea Oil revenues and 20% VAT on increasing prices at the pump should be enough."
AA spokesman Luke Bosdet said: "Drivers are punch drunk with rises over the past few months with some even not taking to the road."
Much depends on how other oil-rich countries, and particularly Saudi Arabia, respond.
Analyst Edward Meir, of MF Global, said: "I don't think Libya alone will take us to $150 a barrel but if unrest spreads in the Gulf countries, we could get there."
The nationwide average for unleaded has soared to a record 128.97 a litre and diesel to 134.34p a litre. Many garages already charge more.
Lockerbie: Pages 8&9

"Many countries have implemented the reduction. I think all of them will implement it because they do not have a choice," said Opec president Chakib Khelil.
The Organisation of the Petroleum Exporting Countries agreed on December 17 to reduce supplies by 2.2 million barrels per day.
"I think this reduction will have an impact on prices in January-February because it is a strong reduction," Khelil said. "We seek to stabilise the price and prevent it from falling further. I think we will reach this stabilisation in January-February, God willing," he added, but gave no forecasts for prices in the next two months.

____________________________________________________________

Why oil crisis could be trigger for a better future: Crude oil prices trading at a record 140 a barrel. Truck driver strikes leading to panic buying at petrol stations across the country. Saudi Arabia promising to pump more oil after desperate calls from world leaders. Ladies and gentlemen, welcome to the global economy's third oil price shock.

Author: Anonymous

Publication info: Anonymous. 

https://ucd.idm.oclc.org/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/why-oil-crisis-could-be-trigger-better-future/docview/335084526/se-2?accountid=14507

Abstract: While acknowledging this is cold comfort for hard-pressed households and oil-dependent businesses, he has said high crude oil prices are "a really good thing" so long as the response is "creative". Wind turbines, solar energy and the organic movement were all born out of a desire to break the world's oil addiction, he argues.

Links: https://JQ6AM9XS3S.search.serialssolutions.com?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Aeuropeannews&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Western+Morning+News&amp;rft.atitle=Why+oil+crisis+could+be+trigger+for+a+better+future%3A+Crude+oil+prices+trading+at+a+record+140+a+barrel.+Truck+driver+strikes+leading+to+panic+buying+at+petrol+stations+across+the+country.+Saudi+Arabia+promising+to+pump+more+oil+after+desperate+calls+from+world+leaders.+Ladies+and+gentlemen%2C+welcome+to+the+global+economy%27s+third+oil+price+shock.&amp;rft.au=Anonymous&amp;rft.aulast=Anonymous&amp;rft.aufirst=&amp;rft.date=2008-06-20&amp;rft.volume=&amp;rft.issue=&amp;rft.spage=18&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=The+Western+Morning+News&amp;rft.issn=&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   Crude oil prices trading at a record 140 a barrel. Truck driver strikes leading to panic buying at petrol stations across the country. Saudi Arabia promising to pump more oil after desperate calls from world leaders. Ladies and gentlemen, welcome to the global economy's third oil price shock.
Yet among the unremitting gloom - Gordon Brown this week declared spiralling oil prices were "the most worrying situation in the world" - there is hope. The Westcountry-based pioneer of a community movement trying to wean themselves off oil argues that it may presage the most positive lifestyle changes in 30 years. Many others agree.
Rob Hopkins, who two years ago founded the first so-called "transition town" in Totnes, South Devon, reckons that the pain being felt at the pumps is already convincing increasing numbers of people to abandon their cars and move towards walking and cycling, growing their own vegetables and shopping locally.
While acknowledging this is cold comfort for hard-pressed households and oil-dependent businesses, he has said high crude oil prices are "a really good thing" so long as the response is "creative".
A modern history lesson helps. Mr Hopkins drew comparisons with the oil shocks of the 1970s and early 1980s. The sudden rationing of oil by key members of Opec not only resulted in lower speed limits to conserve the precious natural resource but also an unprecedented burst of groundbreaking ideas. Wind turbines, solar energy and the organic movement were all born out of a desire to break the world's oil addiction, he argues.
He said: "There is something about oil prices that focuses the mind. We have been aware of climate change for years but it has not stimulated anything like that. Necessity is the mother of invention."
The cause of today's oil panic may be different from that 30-odd years ago. In 1973, key Arab producers boycotted oil exports to the US and their Western European allies for supporting Israel in its conflict with Syria and Egypt. Today a murky alliance of China's breakneck growth, "peak oil" and market speculators is at play.
Even so, the ramifications could be similar, but not just in terms of filling stations raising fuel prices to almost pounds9 a gallon for petrol and diesel as one retailer in Exeter did this week.
"If you had not had that period in the 1970s, wind power would have been in its infancy. Solar would have been primitive. It is a bit like Sleeping Beauty. We have been asleep through the 1980s and for 28 years. Now we have been pricked awake," said Mr Hopkins. "What we are seeing now is really exciting."
A teacher of natural building, Mr Hopkins says it was awareness of the end of the age of cheap oil - known as peak oil - that triggered the "transition" movement.
Hundreds of people in Westcountry towns and villages, including Falmouth in Cornwall and Seaton and Ashburton in Devon, have been drawn to its principles: using public transport rather than filling their cars, reducing the distance food is transported and local production of goods and services. As many as 700 towns cities and villages have joined, mainly in the UK but also as far afield as Australia.
Mr Hopkins cited the trend for growing vegetables in back gardens, spiralling sales of seeds and the revival of making your own clothes as indicators of how habits are changing.
He recently met a woman on a train who had never travelled by rail before but had opted against the car because it was now too expensive.
It is not just about saving money, he contends. A world not reliant on temperamental oil supplies, which we rely on for everything from clothes to medicines, could be a much happier place. Some of the more unsavoury aspects of modern life are underpinned by oil: "We are working longer hours than in previous generations, less time with our family, more overweight."
Mr Hopkins, hailed by commentators as a post-oil visionary, added that he did not want to rejoice in the face of widespread misery, acknowledging that "this is really starting to hurt people, particularly those businesses that are oil dependent".
But he went on: "It is important to make the point that the more oil- dependent we are the more vulnerable we are. That vulnerability is only going to grow. The age of cheap oil is finished. EasyJet has said the age of cheap flights is over.
"There is something big happening. It is difficult and we are asking some very tough questions of ourselves. But at the same time we have a choice. We can look at this as an opportunity."
Asked whether he had predicted that oil prices would touch 140 a barrel so quickly, he said: "Yes. I'm not surprised. It was blindingly obvious. People like Goldman Sachs are talking about 200 dollars a barrel sooner or later."
Westcountry groups have reported more interest in recent months. Cathy Debenham, a spokesman for Sustainable Ottery, a group of people in the East Devon town of Ottery St Mary who had joined the transition movement, said more than 150 people came to its launch last month.
She said: "It is easier to persuade people to get involved when you see it every time you fill up your car with petrol, or every time you get a bill.
"I have known for a long time that driving at 70mph or less saves you money and petrol. But it is only in the last month or so that I have started measuring it. And it makes a big difference."
David Mathews, acting chair of Transition St Austell, a like-minded group in Cornwall's clay country, said: "The Government's call for more production is simply madness.
"They should be taking steps to reduce consumption now. One way would be to bring back the speed limit of 50 mph, which was introduced in the oil crisis of 1973-74. Such a limit would reduce fuel consumption, save motorists money and save lives."

Subject: Petroleum industry; Speed limits; Alternative energy sources; Crude oil prices

Title: Why oil crisis could be trigger for a better future:   Crude oil prices trading at a record 140 a barrel. Truck driver strikes leading to panic buying at petrol stations across the country. Saudi Arabia promising to pump more oil after desperate calls from world leaders. Ladies and gentlemen, welcome to the global economy's third oil price shock.

SEN. CARL LEVIN AND SEN. BYRON L. DORGAN HOLD A JOINT HEARING ON SPECULATION IN THE CRUDE OIL MARKET

https://ucd.idm.oclc.org/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/wire-feeds/sen-carl-levin-byron-l-dorgan-hold-joint-hearing/docview/467172941/se-2?accountid=14507
